This is very informative for people who don't know. I already knew a lot of it already. My father worked in USINS. Applying for visas from state department, filing paperwork, getting green cards, etc are all a major pain and are quite expensive. It's gotten even worse over the years. Used to be faster but they have the system all screwed up now. You have to stay on top of them. In the new system if you don't keep checking up every couple months they will claim you lost interest and throw the paperwork out & you have to start all over. As an aside, my best friend bought a car from the angry wife of a guy who got deported back to Honduras because he didn't keep up on his green card paperwork. You'd be surprised at how many guys overseas will file for fiance visas while actually married to someone in their home country. They use US citizens to get green cards, wait until they are fully established as citizens or permanent residents, divorce their US wives, and then bring their foreign wives over. It's part of the reason why the system is such a PITA. If your fiance has been vaccinated for Covid he probably has a better chance of getting over. Fun fact: The largest portion of illegal immigrants in the US are people who entered legally but overstayed their visas. I'm excited for you and hope everything goes smoothly.

Congrats, Kayla!
Congrats! My husband and I went through this whole visa process! It's very frustrating and nerve wracking. We got ours before Covid thankfully but the whole process still took over 3 years for us. Wishing you the best of luck! As long as you can get the travel bans worked out though, the rest of the process should be fairly smoothly for you guys. Small note: the money you have to make for the visa in the US is 125% over the national poverty line based on the amount of people in your family, and they are EXTREMELY picky on that. Our visa was delayed for about a month simply because my husband and I were 3k short based on the previous tax return and they wouldn't accept my current paycheck stubs which my income that year was actually over the limit so my parents had to sponsor him jointly with me if our income fell below that amount which basically they signed a paper saying they would support us for the rest (aka $0 money).

Omg immigrating is a nightmare. I'm immigrating to the US from Canada and it's awful. Having a court marriage ASAP but a wedding party down the road is 1000% valid and acceptable! Dont get married while you are waiting for him to get processed. it will make your case delayed.  The biggest mistake my buddie did who moved to TX from Canada was marrying his now wife in TX.  it delayed their case two years because it sends red flags that it may be a fake marriage to just get citizenship.
My buddie who immigrated here to Canada from the UK had to have 20,000 GBP in his bank account in order to come to Canada.

And us Canadians have free universal healthcare so we arent used to paying for healthcare.  Our healthcard doesn't cover medical to immigrate to a new country,

Kayla, when deciding whether or not to take the plunge and do the 14 day quarantine in another country, dont wait too long. Congrats! I just went through the same process, but I was the one immigrating. My husband and I were in a long distance relationship for 5 years before we applied for the K1-visa. The process is long and stressful. I got my interview date 9 months after we applied in 2018. I came over to the US in August 2019 and got married within a week. Then the temporary green card process.... took around year, but I am a permanent resident now. Now all that's left is the removal of conditions, for the 10 year green card and then after that I can apply for citizenship. The US immigration process is hard and time consuming., but we are happy to finally be together and would do it all over again.

I worked at Home Affairs in Australia within the Visa process and I cannot imagine how stressful it is being an applicant. You have people contacting you daily, even hourly wanting updates on their case but there's nothing you can do even when you're someone who processes them. Unsure about other countries and foreign affairs workers but here in Aus, you feel pretty damn useless. Imagine setting up and paying thousands for a Visa to have someone you love come and be with you. Then being on the application processing side and sending information requests off to other foreign governments and having to wait for the results so you can finally tell someone else who has also waited months they're finally good to go. It is draining to say the least.

Ok but how are you just gonna gloss over the fact that you're engaged! How did it happen? When's that story dropping?
@lilsimsie I went thru the CR1 vis with my husband, we sent in about 5 pounds of evidence of being in a relationship(photos text msges since the start, receipts of gifts we bought each other, hotel registrations that we both stayed at during his business trips to the USA, bank accounts, etc etc etc.). He was only asked 5 questions at his interview  1: How did we met  2: When was the last time we saw each other 3: Where did we see each other last 4 What I did for a living 5: What he did for a living  Other people that were being interviewed at the same embassy had harder questions.  Right now we are preparing for the Removal of Conditions.  I hope his questions are as easy as ours was.   CR1 took from Jan 3rd 2018 till Nov 27th 2018 (interview). We got a RFE at interview for hubs CV so the government could do more in-depth background check, due to the nature of his career. Submit the next day, and got approval mid March 2019.

I hate how long the visa takes. My husband is from Vietnam, but was already in the U.S. on a student visa turned OPT visa. We got married first since he was here already. Applied July 2018, received his work authorization February 2019, and his interview/approval July 2019! Takes FOREVER. The thing that sucks is that if you've been married for less than 2 years when apply for visa then the green card is only good for 2 years and you have to pay more money to have the condition taken off green card. But he can receive citizenship after 3 years on a green card. We just applied for his condition to be taken off and he can apply for citizenship July 2022! The initial application is the worst part (besides maybe the citizenship test), but rest is smooth sailing. Congratulations!!!

i moved here from iran in 2016 finally after FOURTEEN YEARS OF WAITING
CONGRATS KAYAK!!!
i went through this process with my husband. It took forever, i got to skip the k1 visa since i was here in usa on student f1 ( Canadian). Adjusted my status in 2016 after court wedding. Then got my green card 9 months from that date in nyc ( got the interview). Moved to seattle from nyc I had to apply for the removal of condition of green card which was filed a year and half after the conditional green card. ( file early since delay is long) got it barely before the conditional green card almost expired. Some people will be asked to come in for another interview but i got to skip ( probably because first one went well)  Then applied to naturalize this took so long for Seattle field office. for me it took a year and half... so finally 2021 jan i became dual citizen. During this time lol i had 3 pregnancies 2 ended in miscarriages but I honestly thought baby was going to be here before my final interview. I went to the interview 19 week pregnant at the time ! finally done with the immigration journey LOL just got my American passport not long ago because that takes a while to get too. I been living in usa legally since 2010 lol. Good luck! the journey will be long but wroth it .

First of all: congrats!! I know exactly how you feel! We're not in the US, but my husband and I got married in December 2019 a bit before his regular tourist visa ran out. In Austria you apparently have to get married first before applying for the visa. So we did get married and then he had to go back to Japan - and we waited for the visa. But then COVID hit us in March (it usually takes 3-6 months they said) and he didn't get to come back until July, which actually was a nightmare because people weren't allowed to actively travel. So while he had the visa and from Austrian side he was allowed to come, the Japanese airline didn't want to let him out of the country because they were scared he could end up stranded on the airport or something... Cue to me, trying to reach *someone* from the government, airport, or something similar, to get an "okay" that the Japanese airline requested, two hours before take-off. The stress I can't tell you... But now he's here and all is well and I am sure it will be fine for you, too! Good luck and fingers crossed the travel goes over smoothly!

Congratulation Kayla!  I am glad that things are moving forward for you and Dan.  I went through almost the same process as you when I got married,  you just have one extra step (and a pandemic) that I did not have to deal with.  It is indeed a long process and very expensive.  But you will get there. Take it in strides and celebrate each step forward. There is need to rush to the "wedding day", and please do not feel pressure by your family, and certainly not social media comments, to do things quickly.  Marrying someone from a different country is an exhausting process.  Give yourselves time to enjoy each other, you will already be legally married in court anyway for the process to continue, and when you are both rejuvenated THEN throw the celebrations! Best wishes!

Congrats Kayla!
I was supposed to get married last May. We had a year and a half engagement and a huge party planned. We were so close when everything shut down. Even if we wanted to get married on our wedding date, courts weren't open. It took us a month and a half to get a marriage license, and our wedding was officiated by our city council member because DC wasn't processing new officiant licenses and we didn't want to be married by a justice of the peace over a zoom call. We eventually got married last June in my friends backyard with immediate family present, but getting to that point was a nightmare. It took a month and a half for them to process our marriage application and 5 months for them to process our marriage certificate. I got married in June and I am still trying to get everything updated to my married name.   I had a truly awful pandemic engagement process, but it was a walk in the park compared to your experience. I'm so sorry! Ironically, getting my new passport with my new name was one of the easier bureaucratic  processes I've gone through in the last year. I'm glad that you can see the light at the end of the tunnel! Congratulations!!

Congratulations!!!   I recently had to go through getting a Danish residence permit based on family reunification to be with my boyfriend at the time and our daughter in Denmark & it was a nightmare. I applied in January 2020 in the US (this was my 3rd application & the other 2 times I applied in Denmark, but I got a lawyer to appeal the decision & they were terrible & pretty much did nothing). Anyways my application was rejected in September because they said we haven't lived together for 18 months (you either have to be married or have been living together and we have been living together since November 2015 before our daughter was born so we thought it was fine). We decided let's just get married so we appealed the decision, got married in December 2020, and my residence permit was finally approved in February 2021.

I'm not usually one to post comments, but congratulations!  The K1 visa is a monster to tackle, and I speak from experience. My now husband is also from the UK. We filed in November 2017 and we got married 19 days after he entered the country in October 2018. He really struggled with not being able to work while we waited for his EAD and AP, and then there was a delay with his actual green card BECAUSE SOMEONE DIDNT THINK BRITISH BIRTH CERTIFICATES WERE ISSUED IN ENGLISH (I'm fne, still bitter, but fine). In May, we'll be applying for his 10 year GC and I think this coming October we'll be able to apply for his citizenship.  It's a gruelling process, but what matters most at the end of the day is that you're with your loved one. Congratulations again! I know you both must be estatic!

Aww I'm so happy for you Kayla!! If you ever feel pressured or anxious about planning your wedding and setting the date and at all jazz, hear me out....Ready?   You don't need to have a big, elaborate, instagramable wedding. This is the 2020s! One of the major struggles newly weds have during their first year of marriage is debt because they decided on taking out $50,000+ worth of loans to plan this ONE DAY event, plus week-long getaway at a private resort or whatever. My husband and I got married 3 weeks after I finished college back in May 2020. Due to the pandemic, we didn't want to run the risk of having people coming to our wedding and then get sick afterwards. We opted to just go down to the county clerk office to obtain our marriage license together, have a small civil ceremony to legalize our union, then get it processed in the records immediately afterwards. The best part? It only costed us less than $200 altogether. My parent did throw us a small party at their house to celebrate and take wedding photos, but overall we didn't go into debt. And now 10 months later, we moved to a new state, we have a house together, a brand new truck, two car titles in our names, we're both working adults, no kids (yetðŸ˜‰), and we're financially stable where we are now.  Moral of the story, do not get you and Dan into a situation that will cause a rift in your relationship. Keep it simple, affordable, and memorable. Other than that, I'm happy for the both of you and I wish you both the best!!ðŸ’–
